A refreshing Sunday means, a plan for have some aromatic age old Mughal Delicacies. Oh yes, you guys are always predict it correctly... Biriyani !!!

Since my childhood, l heard a lot about ‚Äú‡¶∞‡ßü‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶≤‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶∞‡¶ø‡ßü‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßÄ ‡¶Ü‡¶∞ ‡¶ö‡¶æ‡¶Å‡¶™‚Äù from my ancestors. Now time to try it. 

Heard rumours, that the new restaurant of Royal, recently open to the customer at Park Circus, is not at per with their age old quality, like the old outlet at Barabazar. It is almost opposite of Nakhoda Mosque at Ezra street (Rabindra Sarani).

Don‚Äôt expect a valet parking under the hotel. On Sunday you can park your vehicle infront of Royal (2 max), if you are lucky (it is first come first serve basis), because you will find most of the shops closed at Barabazar. I am not so lucky, so my driver parked my car at a distance.

You have to climb a tough narrow staircase to reach the actual restaurant. For the aged people like my parents will find it really tough. After finish climbing you will find non-ac restaurant at your left and ac restaurant at your right. We had choose ac one, because right is always right ;)

The seating zone is not spacious. We had occupied a six seater table, since it was the only option to us, though we were only three.

We found senior attendees wearing grey safari, who are responsible for taking orders. We ordered three plates of Biriyani, Murg Malai Kebab (as starter), Mutton Pasinda Kebab, Mutton Chanp and Sahi Tukra (as desert).

1. Murg Malai Kebab: Oh, it‚Äôs heavenly. Please do try it. Anyone familiar with Arsalan‚Äôs special cheese reshmi kebab can guess it. But it is not so cheesy and not unhealthy as well. If you want to taste real Malai Kebab, here you go. My rating 4.8 out of 5.

2. Mutton Biriyani: Really maintained their dignity. Quality was awesome, I will say, it is in top 2 on my list of Biriyani Houses I had already tried. Quantity too enough for a normal person like me. People with higher appetite will find it bit less and lower (like my mom) find it much more. Of course there you will not find the humble Bengali potato and glossy egg. It‚Äôs the dignity which they are still trying to maintain and a Biriyani enthusiasts like me, will always respect this. My rating is 4.6 out of 5.

3. Mutton Pasinda Kebab: Really awesome, please don‚Äôt forget to try it once. I can swear, you will fall in love with it. Shredded mutton kebab, you will find it look similar with mutton chnap, but can easily distinguish by its boneless feature and different colour. My rating is 4.8 out of 5.

4. Mutton Chnap: I will say, the only restaurant in Kolkata who is still maintained the quality of actual chnap. My rating is 4.5 out of 5.

5. Sahi Tukra: Also a must try item. You will never regret if you try it. The best ever Sahi Tukra I ever tried in my life. My rating is 4.8 out of 5.

After completing my Biriyani survey, I will revisit some of the Biriyani houses. Royal should be one among them for the entire life, till it maintains its quality.

2017-11-07 18:41:29
Arnab Chatterjee
31783977
5.0
One of the famous & legendary mughlai restaurants of Kolkata , Royal Indian Hotel , has been serving the foodies for a long time . Situated on Rabindra Sarani near Nakhoda Mosque this place is renowned for their delicacies throughout the country . The locality is very congested & parking is an issue in the narrow roads . The restaurant has remained the same since I first visited here more than 30 years ago as a little boy clutching my parents fingers . The beautiful smell of mughlai cuisines will greet you as you approach the place . The ground floor is mainly the takeaway section though some seating arrangements are there . If you are visiting with your family then the first floor family section is a better option . Though it lacks the glitz of today's modern restaurants but the place is reminiscent of the old days when Kolkata used to be Calcutta & separate family cabins with Purdah add to the nostalgic feeling . The staffs are well conversant with the foods on offer & will explain to you in detail about the preparation of the dishes . Coming to the food today we had the following :
Chicken Tikka Kabab : We ordered Chicken Tikka Kabab as a starter & it was mouthwatering . A plate contains 7 pieces of Kababs with associated salads , a perfect dish to begin our journey .
Mutton Biryani Special : A visit to Royal is never complete without their Biryani . We chose the Special one as it contains two pieces of mutton . The Royal Biryani is devoid of potato & egg & follow the traditional Lucknowi style . The quantity is sufficient while no words can describe the splendid nature of quality of the Biryani . The aromatic rice combined with the perfectly cooked mutton is a sheer delight .
Mutton Chap : Another famous dish of Royal . The small mutton pieces are great in taste & its a sheer pleasure to close the eyes & savour the taste . The gravy is truly mesmerizing when taken with a roti .
Mutton Tikia : Hardly ever had a better Tikia anywhere else . The minced mutton with adequate & right quantity of spices was another high point .
Rumali Roti : The perfect companion for Chap & Tikia . The roti was light & fresh , the grain used is of high quality .
Firni : The great dessert after a royal mughlai meal . Firni in an earthen pot completed our meal for today.
Royal Indian Hotel was truly royal when I visited here with my parents , still is royal when I am visiting with my wife & will no doubt remain as royal as ever when we will take our son with us in near future .
Highly recommended .

##

2017-11-06 15:24:42
Sayantan Ghosh
34553906
5.0
I have always wanted to write about the Royal Indian Hotel, which introduced the dish which would later transcend the boundaries of age, race, caste and religion to become the most popular delicacy of Kolkata - biriyani. Ahmed Hussain, was a migrant wrestler from Lucknow with a passion for cooking. His ancestors were chefs in the royal kitchens of Awadh, and it is said that their secret biryani recipe was handed down the generations in Hussain's family. He rented a small space in Chitpur from Raja Rajendra Mullick of the Marble Palace, Kolkata and opened up the Royal Indian Hotel in 1905. Today, over 110 years later, the original branch of this restaurant still stands at the same place in Chitpur.

The place caters to a range of customers, with two non-AC halls (one on the ground floor, and the other on the first floor) and a slightly more expensive AC hall on the first floor.

The menu is short and crisp - you know exactly what you want to order, anyway! Let me talk about a few of my favourties:

1. Royal Mutton Biriyani: Starting off with the obvious, Royal serves my favourite biriyani in Kolkata (with the possible exception of the Saffron at Park Hotel, but then, I can't afford Saffron every week). The biriyani is light, and less spicy than your average Kolkata biriyani, and less fragrant. The reason is these guys do not use cinnamon. Cardamom, clove and saffron are used to give the biriyani its subtle flavour. However, due to the less aromatic spices, the wholesome and tantalizing aroma of the basmati rice is well-preserved and pervades your surroundings when the plate of biriyani is put in front of you. Contrary to the Kolkata tradition, there is no potato in the biriyani. This makes sense, since the potato was supposedly an innovation of the chefs of Nawab Wajid Ali Shah during his exile years in Calcutta, since the Nawab's household could not afford enough pieces of meat at that time (it was basically a cost-cutting innovation). The mutton is cooked just right for the meat being tender enough, while preserving the original juiciness and flavours of the meat. The rice is light and fluffy, and not too greasy (unlike standard biriyani). The taste is more subtle than your regular biriyani, and in general, and the taste gently spreads over your taste buds rather than assaulting them.

2. Chicken Tangri Kabab: The drumstick-only cousin of the popular tandoori chicken, the kababs are always well-grilled. The pieces are just very slightly chewy on the outside, but soft on the inside. The pieces are well marinated, and you can taste the tandoori spices well into the core. There is no sweet cream or malai added (like they do in kalmi kabab in some restaurants), so the kabab remains tangy and spicy.

3. Chicken Curry: I prefer this gravy item to go along with my biriyani instead of the more popular Mutton Chaap of Royal. The gravy is exceptionally light for an Indian curry, seasoned with minimal spices. The oil content is also comparitively much lower. The comparitive subtlety of the gravy actually makes the taste of the chicken more pronounced. The chicken piece is tender and juicy, with the original meat flavours well-preserved. They also serve a large piece of potato in the curry, which, for me, compensates for the absence of the potato in the biriyani.

4. Shahi Tukda: Not being a fan of the phirni, I love this piece of ghee fried bread covered in rich sweet kheer (condensed milk), flavoured with saffron and garnished with chopped almonds. Available on only a few of days of the week at Royal, this rich dessert is the perfect way to end your biriyani meal.

The staff is quite courteous and always ready for assistance whenever required.¬†
The ground floor has a huge hall adjacent to the kitchen, where the seating capacity is almost about 100 and is quite spacious. The top floor has a capacity of more than 100 seating & AC along with it.

Items Ordered:¬†
Main Course: 2 Plate Royal Mutton Biriyani¬†
Desert: 2 Plate Firni
Cost: Rs.505 (Including GST)

The bill comes only with the price that is printed in the menu card.

The quantity is very less as compared to the amount they are charging for per plate. And more over the history of Royal always says that it serves one of the best & lip smacking Biriyani in town, but somehow I didn't feel enough charm in their taste.

The place is best for one time dining.
Cost for two: Rs.500 approx (Including GST)

If they increase the quantity of the platters (*specially the Biriyani) and re-generate the the long legacy which they used to have in their taste, the hotel will truly be "The Royal"!

##

2017-10-14 15:23:03
Pramit Saha
31717307
4.0
Royal Indian Hotel is one of the pioneer of Biryani in Kolkata. 
Wajid Ali Shah, the last Nawab of Awadh came to the Kolkata suburb of Metiaburj in 1856 after defeated by British. But he did not forget bringing his personal Chef with him as he was very particular about his food. Form the Rasoi of Nawab Kolkata Biryani started its journey. The Baburchi used to add potatoes and eggs along with meat in Biryani which was served to the working class people under Nawab. But the Nawab always had the authentic Awadhi Biryani which had cooked only with Gosth or meat. Royal Indian Hotel is one who maintain this Nawabi Biryani style.
Let's come to the food.

1.Mutton Biryani: The name doesn't need more descriptions. Royal serves authentic Biryani. It consists a good quantity of flavored rice and a soft piece of mutton. Taste.... Please come and try.
 
Note: they don't add ALU or Egg in Biryani

2. Chaap (Chicken and Mutton): If you asked any one where to go for chaap ...only one answer you will get...Royal. Meat cooked in ghee keep you licking your plates.

3. Sheek kebab: Good size of kebab served with green chutney.

Service: For Biryani you don't have to wait.For Kebab, it depends. Overall service is good.

Food: 4.3/5
Service: 4/5
Ambience: 3.8/5 

N:B: For good ambience I  prefer its new Park Street brunch opposite Quest Mall

I visited Royal more than five times and wanna visit again for the Chaap.

2017-09-10 15:04:59
Abin Basu
307471
4.5
Perfect genuine authentic awadhi biryani- that's what Royal is all about. No artificial smell, no artificial colour- that's the hallmark of awadhi biryani & that's what differentiates it from calcutta style biryani.. You can get the mild & sweet aroma that is of pure saffron & basmati. the rice have a very mild yellow colour that comes from saffron only. The piece of mutton is perfectly tender. And along with that adequate amount of ghee/dalda & very little amount of spices- Royal has indeed maintained the genuinity of awadhi biryani through out these years. People expecting to have calcutta style biryani might feel a little disappointed here because there is no big piece of potato or egg that can be found & hence the quantity might seem a little less. But for me it was adequate. They have both ac & non ac segment. Though you might have to wait a little as most of the times it is crowded & the ambience seems mediocre. But as a biryani lover i can say that it is worth everything & must visit place.

2017-09-08 22:17:58
Sankha Subhra Ghosh
37035867
4.5
It can't get simpler than this. Go to Royal. No need for any menu card or second thoughts. Simply ask for the Biriyani and Chaanp. Obviously mutton!! (What else?? Chicken is ONLY for Kabab, right? For anything else it should be Mutton or Lamb or Beef. Well, in very few cases you may consider pork also. but that's another discussion altogether) Yes!! That's it. 

Now just wait and watch till they bring you that magical plate covered with yellowish rice with aroma vaporizing out of it. A small plate full of small small pieces of Chaanp will accompany it and you can easily feel the coriander plus ginger cooked in ghee smell has already taken you under its spell.

Savor them slowly. Relish the moment with each morsel. Everything in the world can wait. Royal offers little spicy Biriyani, mostly flavored with black pepper, nothing you can't handle. This makes the taste class apart from the regular average bi-color Biriyani you'll get every corner and some so called big names. Oh and don't insult Biriyani expecting egg and/or that dreaded hand grenade size potato. Who eats that potato now a days I wonder!

Only Aliah can come closer in comparison to Royal. It will be a tough competition.

If you are extra hungry, and in the mood for appetizer, you may go for Sugandhi Kabab. but trust me, they are not that good.

If you want to try something new, Pasinda kabab is your best bet. Its again a mutton preparation, similar to Chaanp, but little sour in taste and sometimes I really have hard time to decide between Pasinda Kabab and Chaanp. Chaanp gets the benefit of doubt most of the time :)

For dessert, Firni can be an option. Shahi Tukra is great too, but bit sweeter for my taste. But I hardly ever order them. Biriyani and Chaanp is good enough for me most of the times. I eat less but it has to be the best ;)

4.0
If you are at Borobajar and really hungry, then there is only one address to go to - Royal Indian Hotel. It is very near to Nakhoda Masjid and is not difficult to find. This place is simply legendary and you might even hear your grand parents talk about "Royal" with a special mention about their "Chaap". I had the good fortune to visit this place today and hell yeah, I was satisfied. They have an air-conditioned seating area upstairs which is preferable if you are with your family. The menu is short. We decided on mutton biriyani, chicken chaap, tandoori roti, roomali roti, salad and firni. Firstly, biriyani was excellent, just the way I like it, mildly scented with a succulent piece of mutton. On the down side, there is no potato (for some it could be a deal-breaker), no egg and the quantity seemed quite less when compared with other biriyani joints. But taste wise it is great. The chaap is very nice too. I was a little disappointed with the firni. It tasted ordinary. But overall it was a hearty meal at Rs 520 for 2 people. If I do visit that area again i will surely visit Royal again, to try their mutton korma.

2017-08-03 10:42:23
Vesper Lynd
40523977
4.0
Hav been to dis place quite a few times. Their biriyani is devoid of any aloo but dey make it up with the topping of koftas(meat balls). It was on my first visit to this restaurant, that they messed up as they had run out of the meatballs. But otherwise the biriyani is an absolute bliss and the ingredients used in it are genuine. They supposedly dont use any artificial colourants, but carrot extracts to colour their rice. The serving of meat was generous and tender. Overall Royal can be certified as one of the best biriyani joints in Kolkata.
Coming to their mutton chaap; tastewise i dont remember if i had tasted a better chaap else where but ingredientwise it was 25 pc meat and 25 pc bone , 25 pc animal fat floating in 25 pc dalda with the right spices added to it and cooked to perfection. So i guess u got wat i mean. Tasty: yes
@Value 4 money: not at all
(Can make u really sick if u dnt leave behind da dalda)
The firni is a delight to have though, perfect consistency nd taste; no complains against it!
Staff is amateur, they have little children filling up ur glasses and cleaning the table(thats supposed to be illegal ). There are senior staffs as well, they might not be highly groomed but are polite and so is their manager. On our second visit we wer done with our meals and about to leave but it was raining heavily outside. Even though the restaurant was jampacked the manager offered us to sit at our table till it stopped raining and this was an unforgettable gesture.
The washroom is equipped,clean,hygenic and has a air of mughal splendour in its decor.
One thing one needs to be careful about is that they serve you the salad without asking your permission; we thought it was complimentary and took 2 slices of cucumber from it on our first visit and they charged us for the whole salad! So anyone who dont need a salad just ask for it to be removed from your table before you start with your meal.

##

2017-07-16 16:19:04
Rajarshi Barman Roy
5869891
2.5
This is the probably the oldest mughlai/awadhi restaurant in Kolkata, but it's location being a constraint for me, had never visited till 8th July 2017. So, after our quick snack attack at golbari in the evening we reached this place at 8 clock.
It is located right in vicinity of the nakhoda masjid. The nearest metro station is mg road. Finding parking beside it will be a wee bit difficult.
We reached this place and saw a huge line of people at the takeaway. The aroma emanating from their kitchen was nothing less than a poetry!
We hopped up the stairs quickly to get ourselves seated in the AC portion of the restaurant and placed our order in no time. The restaurant is nothing much to look at; Comfortable sofas with normal decor, perfect for heavy dining.
Anyhow, my friends and I, especially was famished. So we ordered a plate of chicken tikka kebab and bada kebab as starters and I settled for a plate of its legendary special mutton biryani for mains with the legendary chicken chap as side. Don't expect a fast n proper service,these people are slow.
The kebabs were served just off the tandoor. Soft , succulent, smoking hot and spicy pieces of chicken tikka kebab was just the perfect start I needed. It was followed by the bada kebab,almost same in flavour, just bigger pieces with bones.
Next was the time for their allegedly legendary pi√®ce de r√©sistances.
I always have this extra love for the awadhi variation of biryani , always so flavour full, not overwhelming and yet subtle in the use of the spices, making it outstanding in the biryani category. So I had high hopes from them.
However,my hopes were shattered in no time!!

1st the biryani even though looked stunning didn't smell stunning at all. 2nd of all it was dry, anyone knows a perfect awadhi biryani can't be dry at all, it should have a perfect coating of ghee/dalda. 3rdly the pieces of mutton albeit big and soft wasn't juicy, they were devoid of any moisture content in them. 4th, being an ardent lover of biryani that I am, I need the quantity right, yet their quantity was considerably less. It fell short on many points, however there wasn't any infernal alu/potato in the biryani that was a saving grace. The rice quality was fine too. But the biryani wasn't even near to my expectations, rather I shall rank it in the near top of my worst tasted biryanis ever!
The chicken chap, was also not my liking; again a heavy dry gravy with lots of oil and a dry thin piece of chicken leg!
Anyhow, with all my expectations dashed, we left the place with heavy heart.

PS it cost 800 for 2 ppl.

2017-07-06 19:50:03

4.5
This one is the shining jewel of North Kolkata. In the midst of always busy Bara bazaar area, no one can miss this place. Just a 5-8 minute walk from Mahatma Gandhi metro station, a person can easily reach their. About the food, it stands it's reputation of being the oldest awadi biriyani restaurant of Kolkata. The biriyani engages in a aromatic battle as soon as you put it in your mouth. The mutton keema served is quite oily but taste is just lip smacking and it goes well with tandoori roti/ rumali roti. The chicken kadai served did have it's own unique taste in a good way. And as we know, a good biriyani story should always end with a firni as a icing but it wasn't able to leave it's mark. As a whole, a place that you really need to visit with your friends/family. BTW, it's light on pocket.

2017-07-06 14:28:05
Madhurima Adhikari
33534851
4.0
My friend is an absolute fan of Royal's biriyani and on his constant persistence we decided to order from the same on a rainy afternoon. We ordered via Swiggy from the bara bazar outlet. 
We had ordered mutton biriyani, butter naan, mutton kasha and mutton chap. Sadly they had run out of shahi tukda. 
The mutton biriyani was fragrant and not dry. It did not have any potato (my heart broke a little) but instead had meatballs. The meatballs were richly flavoured and soft. The mutton chap is just the right accompaniment with the rice. It had subtle but amazing flavours and taste. The fat of the dish is what makes it taste even better. The meat was tender and juicy. The naans were how a good naan should be, fibrous yet soft. The mutton kasha was spicy and went very well with the naans. 


Complete bliss!

5.0
I've been eating here since I was 5. Now I'm 22. Sunday, Wednesday and Friday is Pasinda Day, Thursday is Chicken Bharta, Tuesday you can go for Mutton Handi and Mutton Chaap is amazing on any given day. Authentic awadhi salli(gravy) and cooked to perfection. Quantity maybe a little less compared to other places but the "Zaika" is worth it. DO NOT TAKE YOUR CAR. Ideally, Uber and then end the lunch with Kesaria Firni or Shahi Tukra on selected days. The staff is revered for their "tehezeeb". They'll refer to you as 'Aap' no matter what your age and background.

Mutton Rezala: cannot complain about the meat (or its colour here!). It was perfect. The food was simply regal.

##

2017-02-26 10:25:40
Utsav Ganguly
2537814
4.5
Located in the busy Nakhoda Mosque area of Chitpur, Royal Indian Hotel is one of the ooldest biryani joints in town. IT serves Awadhi biryani instead of the more ubiquitous Kolkata biryani which means that it has no potato or egg. Being an ardent lover of the potato in a biryani, this had been a point of slight concern for me. Nevertheless, I visited it for lunch with a few friends. The decor is modest and exudes an old-world charm.

We ordered what a first-timer ought to order here : ¬†the mutton biryani , the mutton chaap and the chicken chaap. All the food reached the table within 5 minutes of ordering which is a huge plus. The biryani has to be one of the best I've had in Kolkata. A perfectly balanced subtle ¬†flavour which does not overpower the palate, I most certainly did not miss the potato in the dish. While the mutton chaap was strictly okay, the chicken chaap had an amazing flavour. They use dalda in their cooking which makes the fats harden up pretty quickly, but it is unlikely your food would last that long, it is that good.

In addition to great, quick service, the value for money here is excellent too. Quite different from the more ubiquitous biryani chains all over Kolkata, Royal still firmly hold its ground in the biryani domain and, I hope, will continue to do so for many more years to come.

2017-02-19 01:53:59
Sudeshna
29217144
3.5
This iconic place certainly needs no introduction! ROYAL is one of the oldest restaurants in Kolkata, started its operations much before the likes of Shiraz, Arsalan, Aminia etc. Had bookmarked this place few months back and siezed the opportunity to drop by while visiting the Bara Bazaar area for some work.

It's bang opposite the Nakhoda mosque, so an easy to locate place. Once we reached there, took a long flight of stairs to the first floor seating area which is air-conditioned. There are also old fashioned non-ac cabins. So people can choose as per their convenience. The food was served within five minutes of placing the order and we dug inüò∏

‚èπRumali Roti - It was how it should it, soft an paper thin.

‚èπMUTTON CHAP - Royal being known for its chap, we decided to go for it. The boneless mutton pieces were succulent, moderately spiced and not too greasy. It's actually difficult to make out where the gravy ends and the meat starts, such is the smoothness. I didn't quite realize at first, but a few seconds into the chap I had already downed two glasses of water, my poor little taste buds were literally onüî•üî•

‚èπCHICKEN BIRYANI - Was compelled to order the Biriyani to get some relief from the mutton chap and I relished every bit. The Biriyani rice here is little more yellow colored, was cooked to perfection, with right amount of spices and mildly aromatic. The huge chunk of the chicken piece was tender and well seasoned. The rice came without the chunk of 'Aloo', (a MUST in Biryanis here in Kolkata) which was a blessing because I always tend to exclude it while ordering. Just a small glitch, the rice didn't seem to be of superior quality as it was missing that extra long fine texture. So, certainly not the best Biriyani I have had.

‚èπFIRNI - It had a creamy texture with mild sweetness. Thus added a nice finishing to our meal!

The food I would say is not exceptional but reasonably priced. Would like to visit this place again to try out other side dishes and of course for it's irresistible Biriyani!! üòªüòª

No potato or egg is involved as they present it in authentic Lucknow style (i guess). I liked it but my friend felt it was rather bland. So taste will definitely vary with people. But that was made up by the rather spicy kadhai chicken. Nothing special again but Well cooked and enjoyable. Roomali rotis, well nothing to write about them, they were brought in as fillers because the quantity of biriyani was just not plenty for Gluttony Hungry MEN. The firni was good and creamy and light. Maybe the firni was the best, and gave the "nothing so special" show a sweet ending.
Despite being good it comes down to average because the name it boasts gradually wanes when we actually go in, and "others" in the market have meanwhile taken up the top spots. If not for repeats ek visit to banta hi hai :)

##

2017-01-01 20:01:37
Petuk Baba
790102
4.5
The name itself describes the heritage of this wonderful place. Royal indian hotel truly delivers everything a true biriyani lover prefers to have i.e. good food, efficient service & ofcourse the old charm of north kolkata.

This place is located on rabindra sarani near nakhoda masjid(10mins walk from mg road crossing). The place has huge sitting arrangements ranging from ground floor to 1st floor with both a.c & non a.c rooms.

We got ourselves the following items:-

1. Chicken malai kebab - Juicy soft malai kebabs served with onions & pudina chutney. The dish had 7pcs. This was just heavenly to gorge upon. The charring didn't overpower the taste & the coating of malai gave a soft spongy bite to it. Recommended

2. Chicken tikka kebab - Again a classic kebab dish for those who love their kebabs spicy. This also had 7pcs & was served with onions and pudina chutney. The kebabs were delicate & the marination of kebab masala was spot on.

3. Rumali roti

4. Chicken biriyani - The biriyani was really the highlight of the meal. Can still imagine the taste & aroma of the rice. The biriyani was extemely light on taste & quantity was just right for a single person. The chicken piece was very tender. They don't serve potato which might not be loved by a person but seriously it could be ignore since the biriyani itself would mesmerise you.

5. Mutton biriyani - Same as chicken biriyani.

6. Chicken bharta - A speciality of this place which was well worth the hype. Very creamy & it would just tantalise your taste buds. Shreds of chicken was served with half boiled egg over a thick creamy coriander based gravy. Loved it spoonful of it. Recommended

7. Royal mutton chap - Very different & unique chap of mutton. Here they serve a bit dry shredded version of mutton chap. The taste just won me over. The mutton was properly cooked & the chap masala was just awesome. Recommended

8. Firni - Classic cold finisher which most of us cherish after a hearty mughlai meal. The firni wasn't too sweet nor too bland which was perfect. It was smooth & properly set.

9. Shahi tukda - To sum this up i would have to say "Simply the best". A hot dessert which i'm sure most of you have had it before but trust me this one takes away the cake. The taste was simply divine & we preferred this over the firni. We even ended up taking another 2 plates of it.

After the long list of items, we were overwhelmed with the quality of food. They charged vat & service tax(since we were seated in the a.c room; not sure about non-a.c rooms). The service stood out for me. The food came in quickly & the attendants were very attentive. The place is also pocket friendly since all the items cost about 2200 INR. They also accept card payments. So all in all please be sure to visit this place to have some royal mughlai experience!!

1284839
4.5
One of the most famous mughlai eateries of a city that takes its Biryani very seriously. Located near Nakhoda masjid (closest metro station : MG Road) you can spot the restaurant very easily. The seating arrangement is upstairs, so u have to take the stairs that, from down there, looks to be going straight to heaven. There is both AC and non AC seating arrangements, normally you will get a seat but you might have a queue on the festival days and main holidays. Once inside you soak in all the different aromas, decide the menu and place the order. Pat comes the delivery, this place has one of the quickest delivery times that I have seen. The food is superb, be it the Biryani or the sides. My recommendation here would be the Mutton chap, cut into small portions (almost looks like shredded) and yes it tastes fantastic, also there is no problem of division and all the bickering about the wrong portions of the meat. In the Biryani, you can go for either Mutton or chicken, but personally I would prefer the Mutton and yes the meat portion that comes with the Biryani is a huge one. Only thing though, they have done away with the Kolkata special Alu. The Mutton rezala here is also a thing of beauty and a must try. Today they were in the mood of distributing free Coke bottles for every plate of Biryani, which was a lovely gesture and u soo need the fizz after such a meal.
One thing that I mind here is the quantity of Biryani per plate, most often I have to order 2 for myself and even my parents today had 1.5 plate each. So yeah that apart everything about this place is very good.
Would love coming back here, time and again.

##

2016-06-27 01:56:28
Ankit Jaiswal
33630143
4.5
Your quest for biryani comes to an end with this more than a century old legendary restaurant, located near Chitpur joint (near M.G. road).

It‚Äôs yet another hidden gem in Kolkata which has become synonymous to quality and legendary muglai cuisine. They serve one of the finest Lucknawi biryani in Kolkata. Though it is located in a very congested area in Kolkata but the food here will make you forget everything.

About the restaurant:
It‚Äôs a two-storied restaurant with different levels. The ground floor is basically for the economy class where you will get the real feel of the place. However, the one at the first floor is little expensive having both AC and non-AC section.

A piece of history:
The owner of this place is said to have descended from the rakhabdars of Nawab Wazid Ali shah. There were basically two types of cooks in nawabs kitchen-Rakhabdar and Khansama. Rakhabdars used to cook only for the Nawab and his family members while Khansama used to cook for everybody.

You will not find any potato or egg in the biryani at Royal since the usage of potato and egg was a sin for Rakhabdars to be used in biryani while it was used by the Khansama‚Äôs to feed others. The tradition is still continued at Royal even today.

Royal‚Äôs signature dishes- ‚ÄúMutton Biryani and chaap‚Äù:
Now talking about the food, I started with their Mutton biryani and mutton chaap as suggested by a friend of mine. The biryani was mild and fragrant and the mutton pieces were so tender that it really melted in the mouth. The best part of the biryani was that it was made from long grained rice and non-greasy which is a problem at other restaurants. The mutton chaap was also very amazing and it tasted nice with the rumali roti. Now I can say that this place serves one of the finest biryanis in Kolkata. The best time to come here is around 12:30-1 pm, when the biryani is freshly made.

I would not recommend to take the parcel since the dishes prepared at this restaurant is made from dalda and it would solidify if not consumed hot.

Heavenly dessert- ‚ÄúShahitukda‚Äù:
Coming to Royal is incomplete without having its signature dessert- ‚ÄúShahi Tukda‚Äù. It‚Äôs a fat, thick slice of bread soaked in rabri and topped with dry fruits. Let me tell that this is one of the finest dessert I have ever tasted and it is one of my personal favourite.

Bottomline:
Frankly speaking I got a mixed review about this restaurant but coming here and trying the dishes changed my mind. Biryani and mutton dishes were better than most restaurants in Kolkata but the Shahi Tukda was somewhat heavenly and it‚Äôs a must try dish in Kolkata. I would love to visit this place again especially for the shahi tukda.

Check out more such food experiences at www. foodworm.com¬† and visit my facebook page at www. facebook.com/foodwormblogs/

2016-06-18 15:28:55
Shreya Bhowmick
2526344
4.5
I came to zakaria street to taste the Ramadan special delicacies from this area.After dropping for jalebis at liyaqat sweets and exploring the beauty of architecture at nakhoda masjid,atfirst we came to aminia outlet opposite to the mlsqu.They said haleem is only available for parcel but not for dining in until 6pm.Me and my friend was too tired and hungry from walking so we opted for an air-conditioned place for the lunch.We came at Royal Indian Hotel.We sat at the air-conditioned area and shared our table with 2 other people.Ambience was nothing special but I still rated them so high just on the basis of amazing food I tasted and the warmth of hospitality here.It's worth it.

We started with the legendary mutton biriyani here.I never thought being a hard-core bangali from kolkata I'll fall head over heels in love with this biriyani.The rice was beautifully flavoured with spices and small meat ballls replacing the aloo.And the mutton boti was so tender..just melting in mouth.
Taste wise this is the best biriyani I've tasted..It was so rich in flavour yet light to eat.I still love aloo in biriyani..but royal left me confused now where should I opt for biriyani when I'm in park circus.(they opened new outlet in that area).200ml coke is given complimentary with biriyani.This was really helpful throughout the heavy meal we had.

Then we ordered the ramadan special mutton haleem with rumali roti.We also ordered half tandoori chicken alongside.

Tandoori chicken pieces were really big but still were smoked perfectly all along not overcharred or underdone anywhere.It had a tantalising aroma and spicy taste..went very well with the green chutney on side.

About the course of haleem and rumali roti..This was the first time I tried haleem.The masala and lemon was given separately.Our server suggested us to add the masala according to our taste and the squeeze the lemon juice.My first experience with haleem was wasn't disappointing at all.The pulses were ground finely to give it a smooth consistency.The flavour was creamy,rich but not too spicy.The bowl of haleem had a very homely comforting touch to it. Here also the mutton pieces were very soft.Soft rumali rotis were perfect accompaniment to it..although I love it so much I digged into the bowl with a spoon and had a lot of it on its own only. :P

Even though we were quite full we didn't miss out the dessert by any chance since it was Friday and we were lucky that their special shahi tukda was available.It was quite big in portion.And about the taste..every bite was like a piece of heaven! It had such a lovely aroma of kesar and ghee..topped with lots of chopped almonds.It had such a beautiful flavour that can't be described in words.One of the best dessert I've ever tasted..It left me drooling for eternity.

Service was very fast..we are thankful that we didn't have to wait much with hungry stomach.Our server was a warm and nice man who listened to all our particular requirements patiently and fulfilled them promptly with a smiling face.It's difficult for me to go to this outlet but surely I'll pay visits to the park circus one many times in future to devour on biriyani,shahi tukda and many more mughlai dishes.

2016-06-10 13:08:56
Sumit Surai
11641
4.0
This is a legendary place as far as Mughlai cuisine is concerned. It's located on a congested one way road, but is absolutely worth travelling for and the trouble.¬† The ground floor dining room is simple non ac, but they do have two dining rooms in the first floor. Unfortunately the better and the AC one remains open only for lunch and dinner. I sincerely hope one day they will decide to keep it open all day. 

Service here is no nonsense and fast. Though they are famous for the biryani and chanp, they make awesome kebabs too. So next time you are there, don't miss ordering a chicken reshmi. Biryani here is served without the potato. It is lighter and very flavourful. Pair it with a plate of mutton chanp (no chicken chanp please. If it is chanp, it has to be mutton). Divine combo. Add the oil of the chanp to the biryani and savour what is truly a royal experience. 

Most of the times I stick to the biryani and chanp here, so have not tried their other dishes much. But tried their Nargisi Kofta once and it was just OK.

For dessert you must, must try their Shahi Tukra. It is undoubtedly the best available in Kolkata. Served in a box with almond flakes and silver varak, it a rich, melt in your mouth experience, which you must never miss when here.

There are few cons too for which I could not give this place the 4.5 I wanted to. Firstly the AC dining room not kept open throughout the day, which I mentioned earlier. If your restaurant is open, it is silly to keep a portion closed. 
Secondly, the quantity of Biryani and its price are moving in opposite directions. What they serve now is hugely overpriced.

In all it is still a great place and the biryani, chanp and shahi tukra will make sure you leave the place happily.

##

2016-05-27 13:00:25
Sayani Bagchi
987242
4.0
The 3 of us visited this legendary restaurant last week. Established in the early 1900s, Royal has been on every foodie's to-visit list, owing to its sheer heritage, food standards and nostalgia associated. 

Location: Bidhan Sarani, a little ahead of the famed Nakhoda Masjid of Chitpore. We had taken an Uber which dropped us right in front of the restaurant. Take a metro/taxi if you would.
Ambience: No nonsense fuss free eatery with options of AC/non AC hall. We chose the AC and nimbly slipped into the lavishly (tackily for some, I daresay) decorated AC section on a sweltering Thur afternoon at 3 pm. It was crowded to the tee, and luckily we found the last and only unoccupied table upon arrival.

Food: We ordered 2 Mutton Biryani, 1 rumali roti, 1 paneer butter masala, 1 mutton liver curry, 1 mutton handi, 2 phirnis and soft drink. The mutton handi was a Thur special and had 2 large pieces, soft and succulent, though the gravy wasn't exceptional: it was a run off the mill north Indian gravy and scored a 3/5. The rumali roti was soft and fresh, the paneer was decent tasting but what surprised me was the paneer quality: soft and moist 8 huge pieces of  paneer dipped in an golden brown butter masala gravy. The dish deserved a 3.5/5 for the sheer quality and portion of paneer. The mutton liver curry was amazing, dark brown in  color, with 5-6 diced pieces of the meat liver. The clear winner however for us was the Mutton Biryani which deserves nothing less than a 4/5. Being quintessential Bangalis, we get touchy about the 'aloo' in the Biryani and wouldn't have it any other way- what's a Biryani without the much beloved melt in the mouth aloo in it, adding to the moistness and aroma of the rice?! But the Biryani at  Royal proved us wrong and how. It didn't have aloo alright,  but what it did have was a fresh, light (meaning not the sickeningly heavy dalda infused taste) fleeting aroma to it, which seemed amazing to even look at, not just taste! Other Kolkata places offering Biryani serve undoubtedly delicious fare, but are set back by the heaviness of the dish, where you cannot move an inch after the meal and feel uneasy for hours after. The most stunning part about Royal's Biryani was that right after the meal, we walked more than 3 kms to reach Jorasanko but not for a second did we feel stuffy, unwell or uneasy: magical indeed! Not only have they maintained their food standards but have also kept the fare authentic to the tee, for a good Biryani (the ones you get served at friends' places on Eid) will give you no heartburns, no acidity, only sheer joy!

Pocket Pinch: We paid only 1400 INR (for 3 people) for all the unbelievable portions of food we ravaged! 
Going back again, when next in town!

2016-05-23 12:24:12
Kamalika Chakraborty
1687227
4.0
Location:Get down @Chitpur Bus stop & walk towards Nakhoda Masjid.2mins walk from the main road.
Food:I think in this age of zomato & all, this is one place which surely doesn't bother about these factors.It's a heritage restaurant & is solely famous for the delicious mughlai dishes offered by them since ages. As usual it was a packed up Saturday afternoon there when 2 of us reached to taste the mutton chaap.
We ordered royal spl mutton chaap, mutton qorma, rumali rotis & firni.
I don't need to describe the chaap. This is one kind which you won't get anywhere in kolkata. Here chaap isn't all about a single mutton piece & some gravy. Rather the meat is pounded & bones & meat are Separated. As a result you eventually end up eating small succulent pieces of mutton & the bones are also almost edible :D
Qorma was also tasty & not at all spicey.Rotis are big so be careful when ordering & firni was good.
Overall a good experience & would love to visit again if not this one but the south kolkata branch of theirs.
I can't offer full marks because they need to upgrade the decor & the ambience quite a bit & also some staffs need to learn manners.

##

2016-04-20 22:47:23
Sayan Chakraborty
383284
4.0
Another tick off from my long wishlist.

As the name suggests, this is one of the most famous and oldest heritage eateries of Kolkata. The place is absolutely chaotic and it is always a challenge reaching there. You can get off in front of Mohd Ali park and then take the lane on the opposite side and then take a right from the Masjid.

Their seating zone is divided into three areas. One which is downstairs is absolutely not recommended as it always remains crowded and busy for the takeaway counter. Upstairs they have two. One is Non AC and it has that old Kolkata feel with the vintage decor and the cabins not prevalent now a days. The other zone on the right is AC. This zone is very simple in terms of decor. A standard room with tables and couches. The seating though is comfortable.

Now coming to their food, the place is well known for their Chaap. The Mutton Chaap we ordered was very tasty but let me add a lot of hidden gems in the city serve equally impressive chaap and hence i wont say it was something extraordinary. The Biriyani though was the star of the night. Starting from the quality of rice to the tenderness of the meat inside to the authentic dum preparation, i thoroughly enjoyed the experience. Let me add the biriyani was not at all oily which is to be appreciated. We also ordered for a portion of Nihari Kofta. This item was a revelation. The curry was simply mindblowing but mind the amount of oil which dominated the dish. The Mutton coating was made to perfection and the blending of Mutton keema and the boiled egg inside was soothing to my tastebuds.

Overall this place is highly recommended for every mughlai food fanatic in the city. A MUST TRY!!!

2016-03-26 21:21:00
Aniket Deb
258448
4.5
I have travelled across the length and breadth of our wonderful country, sampled the layered Biryani at the Nizam, enjoyed the Lucknowi variant in Delhi and Lucknow but nothing comes close to the aroma and taste of the Kolkata Biryani

Royal Hotel belongs to the league of the Biryani legends, one of the jewels in the crown of Kolkata's Mughal cuisine landscape. On a warm afternoon I found myself in the crowded streets of Bara Bazar; braving my way through the hush hush I proceeded to a meal at Royal Hotel

I started off with the Royal Mutton Chaap accompanied with Roomali Roti, the Chaap was delectable sparsely hosting a few pieces of bones which actually enhanced the taste; the gravy was dark, thick and spiced beautifully

This was followed by a portion of Chicken Chaap which was amazing as well. The Roomali Roti fell a bit short of expectations and was slightly dry

I then asked for a portion of Chicken Reshmi Kabab which had a moist buttery texture and melted in my mouth instantly. The phirni was good but slightly thicker than usual 

The service was extremely cordial and it would be wrong for me to not mention Mr Ishrafil who made the experience extremely memorable 

Overall I am impressed as to how some of the restaurants in Kolkata are still maintaining the ethnic flavours which used to draw in crowd a few decades ago; the quality is retained and few dishes have even attained perfection

Cheers!

2016-03-11 23:38:07
Sirsho Bandopadhyay
1018652
4.5
Royal is famous for its Mutton Chanp and it will remain so for ages to come!
Been there recently, after some thirty odd years and found that this tiny place on the oldest road of Calcutta has changed a lot, thankfully for the better! Service at Royal was pathetic. They had this 'couldn't care less' attitude of Indian Airlines in the 80s, which could be translated as, since we didn't go to you, but you have come to us, do have the patience to wait for your turn. That was, find yourself a place to seat and wait till one of our waiters decides to pay attention to you. In a changed time, with three air conditioned dining halls on the first floor, the waiters are attentive now and well behaved! :)
The food hasn't changed though. It's as good as ever. Ordered Mutton Chanp and Rumali roti. It was a trip down the memory lane. The Firni also remains very different from other places, very distinct. A meal at Royal is never complete without a Firni. :)
You may ask, why a 4.5 rating then! Well, with food, you always have the scope to do better!

##

2016-02-12 07:36:03
Sumana Mandal
4644921
3.5
Well, starting up with a confession! This is my first-time visit to this legendary/heritage mughlai restaurant of my city...and yes, it is quite shameful being a die-hard foodie! Have had the chance to eat its biryani a couple of times which my dad brought back home... anyway, Better Late than Never!!!
Location : bit tough to locate it on your own if you aren't a north-calcuttan or aren't well aware of the area (i could have never find it out if i didn't have my friend along..i'm a hardcore south-calcuttan, u see!) Anyway, just ask anyone in and around Chitpur and u'll be sorted!
Decor: the restaurant has three sections; a ground floor seating(non AC), a first floor seating(NON AC) and an Air-conditioned section with modern decor which is clearly a new extension of the heritage structure.. i always prefer to sit in the non AC as i'm not fond of one and i think the food tends to get cold faster under air-conditioner.. (see, how big a foodie i am! :D)
Menu: the menu is not so vast that a poor hungry soul would get lost in it. It's quite compact and clealy specifies the restaurant's specialities which i found out to be of great help for the first-timers like me.
Coming down to our orders which included a chicken biryani, a chicken chap, a mutton chap, a couple of rumali rotis (it was lunch time and they didn't have tandoori rotis which really bothered me coz i don't really like rumali roti much. Minus 0.5) and a Shahi tukda.
Food:
* the chicken biryani tasted fine till the point it was warm which is a couple of minutes after they were served and soon after that it showed its colour, i mean, texture. The soft aromatic rice of the biryani turned harder as it was cooked in dalda/ vanaspati which feels so terrible on the tongue. And we seriously felt the quantity was less too compared to other well-known biryani joints in the city. Minus 0.5!
* the chicken chap tasted good, nothing like any of the chicken chaps i have had before at other places. It wasn't swimming in a bowl full of oil and well, wasn't bland either. The chicken was like melting-into-the-mouth soft, but again cooked in dalda/vanaspati! Minus 0.5!
* Mutton chap: I just tasted a tiny bit of the mutton chap and didn't have the entire portion. my friend had it and he quite liked it.. and he said that it's the best of Royal one can get! this was too cooked in vanaspati though..
* Shahi Tukda: wasn't really thinking of having a dessert but it was our waiter who recommended this one and i thank him dearly for doing so as i might be coming back for this one. It tasted divine on the taste-bud, even though it too was prepared using dalda/vanaspati.. (i hope u guys have already understood my hatred for vanaspati..please get rid of it! It's so harmful!)
Overall impression : according to what i have grown up hearing that this is a heritage mughlai restaurant of calcutta that all true blue foodie calcuttans have heard of/eaten at. But is it really so? I mean by the current food quality, i have real and serious doubt! Or if it's really true then it sure has lost its charm and standard.
*** Some serious piece of advice to the management : please for heaven sake stop using dalda / vanaspati in the preparations.. it doesn't taste good as soon as the food loses its warmth. One can clearly see the solidified white layer of vanaspati over the food and can taste it even better which i swear tastes aweful on the tongue. Taste it yourself guys! And do i have to remind you about the ill health effects of it; the clogged arteries of the heart with fattening layers of cholesterol causing out of vanaspati?!
I surely don't want one for myself ! -_-
Am i coming here again? I have doubts. Maybe yes, for that lip smacking shahi tukda!

##

2016-02-11 22:46:41
Shayeree De Sarkar
33514259
5.0
this is called class..me n my family have been eating from Royal all along..this is the authentic mughlai restaurant..i love royal..their biryani, mutton chap r my fav..once they cooked for my bday also wen i was younger..great family ambiance..wnt mention ne names bt the new restaurants DO NOT stand a chance! my father introduced me to Royal..n i am so grateful..dad speaks abt lot of dishes from years back..n says the standard is same..i know food..so i can vouch for Royal..unlike other places Royal's biryani is so light, nt full yellow and da aroma is so subtle..i can kip on writing abt Royal as its my fav Mughlai Resraurant..all da best..

##

2016-01-07 19:26:37
Pratyusa Bhattacharya
1275523
4.0
The place is located on the lane that goes left from the Bata store , a seven  minute walk away from MG road crossing . The restaurant is also close to Nakhoda Masjid , and the name is prominently visible. The seating on the first floor is preferred , though there are seats on the ground floor as well . The first floor has both A.C. and non- A.C. segments . The air conditioned part if nicely lit , the interiors have warm hues and there are tiny chandeliers hanging on top of the tables . The service is quick , though the staff may be a tad difficult to spot . The royal  mutton  Biryani needs no introduction ! It is one of the best and popular  Biryanis in Kolkata  and deservingly so ! The rice is slightly oily but not excessively , and the spices are well blended into the rice  , giving it a  unique flavour that makes it so special and an absolute must try ! The chicken chaanp however , was served cold , and had a single leg piece of chicken , and the gravy seemed frozen after a while !! Lastly , the Firni here is one of the best I've ever tasted , and comes in the signature tiny earthen bowls , and tastes absolutely heavenly ! If you're a Biryani lover , you can't afford to miss this place !

2015-12-30 00:08:45
Sumitavo Paul
183369
4.0
Royal Indian Hotel located right on busy Chitpur road or rabindra sarani has been serving people of kolkata for ages. The wonderful aroma that fills the area where this hotel is located (from the mutton chaap handi that is cooked almost outside the hotel shielded by glass) - would make you hungry even if you are not. This is one of the joints in Kolkata who prepare Biryani without aloo (pure Lucknowi style) and also the rice is spicy compared to others. Their mutton chaap is the best in the city - hands down. The chaap along with freshly made roomali roti is a pure bliss to the tastebud. The chaap is spicy, oil and full of taste - simply superb. Their gravy items or kebabs are nothing special and are almost similar to other mughlaai joints in the city. The kesar firni is awesome and a must try. Overall - hugely recommended.

The air-conditioned section has more taxes and hence higher prices. The food in both the sections is impeccable though. Love the biryani and chap. Wednesday and Friday, be sure to order the shahi tukra. That is truly royal! Happy eating.

1. The Royal Indian Mutton Biryani ( 3.5/5 )
2. The Royal Indian Mutton Chaap ( 3/5¬† )
3.¬† Rumali Roti ( 2.5/5)
4. Firni (3/5)

5.0
Simply stellar Awadhi biryani, and the mutton chaap! It cometh as rain on a parched desert day. Gloriously succulent, sumptuously savory, perfectly spices to accompany the fragrant aromatic rice of the biryani, so delicately scented with cardamom and saffron. We were there at Ezra Street for Diwali light purchase and were dying of hunger. Suddenly remembered that Royal is nearby and immediately agreed to go. The menu Isa straight one. Will be there again very soon.

2015-10-09 12:28:07
Arindam Majumdar
13744
3.0
This place had been in my wishlist for a long time as I had heard many Calcuttan friends rave about it. So, when I visited Kolkata after quite some time, I did not miss the opportunity to try out the food here.

We ordered Mutton Biryani, Mutton and Chicken Chap, Roti and Mutton Kaliya. The Mutton Biryani was top notch with good and fragrant basmati rice and exceedingly soft mutton pieces. It had a bit extra ghee in it, but given the taste, that might be excused. However, almost all other items were below expectations. The Mutton Chap was below average and unnecessarily greasy, the Kaliya had very little meat and too much oil , the Roti was not served hot, the Chicken Chap was just OK but nothing outstanding. Overall, except the tasty biryani, i found the food a big let-down. I was left wondering how a well acclaimed Mughlai restaurant can live with such ordinary side dishes.

Of course, there is nothing special about the ambience, and none was expected. The service is fast, but not very helpful. When we asked for hot Roti, the waiters did not care to mention that Tandoor Roti is available and gave us cold Roomali Roti-s. The prices are OK, and it came to Rs 1400 for 5 people.

Overall here are my ratings regarding the restaurant :
Ambience - 2.5/5
Food - 3/5¬†
Service - 3/5
VFM - 3.5/5
Overall - 3/5

One can go to the restaurant for trying it out, but I would recommend only the Biryani.

2015-10-03 23:13:04
Amrita Deb
6140791
4.5
Well this is in my Top3 for 'Best Biriyani in Kolkata' along with Aminia and Aahar.
Located in the busy and crowded area of Barabazar  in KOLKATA, ROYAL seduces its customers by radiating the delicious irresistible aroma of their biriyanis and chaap. For the newbies, I must warn you the decor and ambience isn't that great. It's very simple. Infact to a certain extent rustic and banal. But the food more than makes up for it! Their biriyanis are an all time favorite among Kolkattans (Trivia: ROYAL even featured in one of the comics of the famous bengali fictional character Feluda.) 
The chicken chaap is another speciality that complements the biriyani/rumali roti impeccably.(Royal makes very good soft Rumali Rotis)
If you're a true biriyani lover like me I would highly recommend you to try ROYAL if you haven't already. I have been going to ROYAL for the last 10years and I still am not tired of it.
Keep up the good job guys!!

3.0
I personally feel that Royal has become somewhat less worth visiting. Their legendary Biryani and Chaap has taken a turn, and not one for the better. 

Critics and Foodies will tell you that Royal is worth going to because of their food -- and that their poor ambience balances their superb Mughlai. I used to have a similar opinion of the place until recently. Their Biryani now has a little too much Garam Masala and they've started to serve less Chaap than they used to. Honestly, reducing portions of fan favourites is criminal in my book. Their service is as fast as ever though, Biryani arrives at your table a few seconds after you've placed your order.

I'm not saying that Royal isn't good anymore -- it's just that there are better Biryani eaters available now. Unless Nostalgia is your weakness, try out some lesser known joints.

Thanks for reading and pardon me for any grammatical errors I may have made.

##

2015-09-13 12:51:33
Sangita Bhattacharya
1634779
5.0
I have been to this place twice and every time I go , I make myself guilt free state considering the amount of calories that is going to be taken in. One word that can be used to tag this place is " brilliant".
The biriyanis , kababs and the koftas are any day to die for.
The long rice of biriyani dipped in butter are one of the finest ones that my tongue has ever tasted. It will melt in your mouth leaving a heavenly taste behind. The do not serve with a potato or an egg unlike other biriyani joints. But the mutton/ chicken is so soft that even a spoon can dig out the mutton in pieces. The quantity is absolutely for one person and for those who have a problem with gastritis, please do not worry since you will not experience a single burp and the entire course will be digested.
I also tasted their haleem, mutton chap, mutton rezala and chicken hundi.
Each and every item is worth trying. Haleem is found only in the month of ramadan and one plate is sufficient for 2 people.The dal and the meat is blended into perfection.
The mutton rezala is a master piece , although served one piece per plate. Do give it a try. The rezala contained enough of butter, cocomut milk and a piece of mutton which will melt in your mouth instantly.
Mutton chap is basically shredded mutton cooked in a peppery way.
Coming to the dessert, both shahi tukra and the firni scores 10/10. I don't know how do they really make it . Shahi tukra is a bread with malai over it cooked into perfection.
The only disadvantage is the timing , it gets closed at 4 pm and starts again from 7 pm.
I would recommend this place anyday, anywhere, anytime without a second thought.

2015-09-07 10:58:14

4019911
5.0
This is old school stuff. Let me give an advice first. If you haven't been there ,go ..simply go today. There is just an old school charm about this place..the hustle bustle of bara bazar ,the nakhoda masjid in the backdrop which you can see if you peer from the balcony or the non ac room upstairs. This is one of the few places which still has cabins.
 take a date on your risk cause you won't be talking much given how great the food is. One downside is though if there are couples in the cabin they keep on rustling the drapes covering the entry of the cabin. So not much privacy. So maybe not the usual ambience of a pricey restaurant but it has its charm.
Now the food- i will sum it up in one sentence . A friend suffering from liver problem had said "Royal is worth risking your liver for". Its that good..The biriyani is a thorough lucknowi style. And the mutton is the most tender i have had. Savour the smell..its simply delicious..and most of all you won't mind working after having this biriyani..its so light on your stomach..the other biriyanis you have  ,you feel like its a total workout . The mutton chaap is the original reason for it being so famous..and chaap rogan is just mind blowing..they use such a myriad of spices that this is one thing you can't just miss.have the chaaps rogan with the biriyani..its  a great combination.  But the mutton are mashed up into small pieces and the bone to mutton ratio is very high.The tandoor items are great.really tender and succulent..highly recommend the reshmi malai kabab,tandoori and mutton boti kabab..and if you are there on wed,fri,sunday do try the shahi tukra..its a sweet dish high on sugar, but a delight.
P.s - if you come here and have a great meal tip the waiter a tad bit more..and then hold on to him for ever ..he will source you the best food from the kitchen. As i said ,old school stuff.

Its old. Its legendary. And its still the best available. Most may argue in favour of Arsalan or some other vendor but none can match Royal. The rice is thin and well cooked. And yes, its best to take away your biriyani and enjoy it at home in your comfy pyjamas.

4.5
The restaurant is situated in the heart of barrabazar area. So, you have to walk through very congested and traffic strucked roads to reach here. And if you are in search of parking place, simply forget it. This restaurant is at 1st floor of the building. It has elaborated A.C. and Non A.C. sections. But you may have to wait a little to get a sit as the A.C. section is always full. Once you manage to get a sit, the staff will promptly serve whatever you order from their menu.

We ordered Chicken reshmi malai kebab, Royal special Chicken biriyani, Royal special Mutton biriyani, hicken chaap, mutton chaap, Green Salad and sahi tukra. And i have no doubt to tell that it is one of the few restaurants in kolkata, which will pamper your test buds to such extent that you forget everything else. Biriyani was very mild spiced contains a large piece of chicken in chicken biriyani and three - four medium to small pieces of meat in mutton biriyani, but it does not contain any potato or egg. Chicken chaap was the best among i yet experienced. Mutton chaap was also very good, but there was too much bones in it. Chicken reshmi malai kebab was the best kebab that i ever had till date. Soft, buttery, juicy, delicious. As they does not serve raita, we had to order green salad, but this salad contains 90% onion. Their saahi tukra was full of ghee, and not creamy in texture and does not contain any gravy. You can find Shredded almonds sprinkled all over this delicious desert.

Now what are you waiting for? Go, and satisfy your taste buds.

##

2015-05-13 02:30:47
EssEmm
10141131
5.0
Eating at The Royal Indian hotel has more to do with my feelings rather than the food. Here's presenting a review which is bound to be biased because this is where my non-vegetarian eating habit was born. 
Situated in a bustling street, the location is the unalluring part of the experience. The hotel has three types of seating areas available. One on the ground floor (near the main kitchen) and two on the second floor (Non-AC and AC). The ambience is extremely basic and can often be termed unsophisticated. But The Royal Indian Hotel and alikes are maestros known for tickling your tastebuds with their food! 
Chicken Biryani, Mutton Biryani, Chicken Curry, Chicken Chaap, Chicken Liver, Mutton Keema, Chicken Reshmi Kebab, Chicken Tikka Kebab, Roomali Roti and Shahi Tukda are the ones that I have developed a taste for in all these years of my visit. 
The biryani has an evident savour which every Royal loyalist relishes. This is one of the few places in Kolkata that does not serve potato in their biryani, and I presume that is another attribute that adds to the distinct taste. The Chicken Chaap has a thick texture with deep flavour of blended spices. The soupy Chicken Curry is a personal favourite as a combo with the biryani. One might complain about the extra fat in the gravies but that can be skimmed easily. Shahi Tukda has been my very recent discovery here, needless to say that it kept my tastebuds happy. 
The parcel facility draws a lengthy queue on most days. The packaging is simple and I have personally not come across any serious wastage due to leaks. Not the healthiest option for good food yet one that I can in no way shun. A perfect tasty meal for the cheat day of a Royalist! (term courtesy Ms.

##

2015-03-28 10:16:08
Indrajit Lahiri
542545
4.5
Previously, I‚Äôve posted something about the generic biryani scenario in Kolkata. And out of them, very few joints have proved to be synonymous with quality and legendary food. And even fewer have been able to come up to such a level that stories are written on it and research has been conducted on them. Royal Indian Hotel in chitpur is one such place. 

How to go and when to go:

If you‚Äôre travelling via M G Road, go towards howrah station and get down at the nakhoda masjid stoppage. Turn towards nakhoda masjid and follow the tram line. Opposite to the mosque, there lies The Royal Indian Hotel. Those, who‚Äôre coming from Lalbazar/ Poddar court, an even interesting ride awaits them. Get on any tram towards chitpur and relax. It‚Äôll drop you bang in front of royal. Ask him to wake you up at Nakhoda. This place is open on all days 11 AM ‚Äì 1030 PM. But, better go early.

Entrance and ambience:

In this place, its a 2-storied restaurant, 1st floor being little expensive. even first floor is having one AC and non-AC section. I personally prefer always the AC family section on the right side. The staircase is pretty steep and tough for any person with knee problem. No lift.

Food:¬†

For food, I should not reinstate that its purely mughlai cuisine here. The owner of this place is said to have descended from the rakhabdars of Nawab Wazid Ali shah. Hence, all the items will have a subtle difference in taste from most other run-of-the-mill joints in Kolkata. For example, Biryani here dows not contain the mandatory Aloo and Egg. Do not get surprised or do not even fall off from the chair. Its true. The Biryani is having little history tucked in it. 

They say when Nawab Wazid Ali Shah came to Kolkata, he was allotted a yearly stipend of INR 12L PA by the british government, which was quite a hefty sum that time. But nawab being nawab, he used to have a huge team of assistants with him and lots of other people to take care of on a daily basis. And that sum was not really that huge as compared to the number. Now, In nawab‚Äôs kitchen, there were 2 types of cooks- Khansama and Rakhabdar. Khansama used to cook for everybody and Rakhabdar used to take care of only the Nawab and his immediate family members. Now as it was getting difficult for the khansama to feed everybody a good amount of meat with the biryani, he introduced the use of aloo/ potato and boiled egg to increase the quantity but it was a sin for the Rakhabdars. And as time went by, Khansamas spread thoughout Kolkata and Kolkata Biryani was introduced, which won hearts of millions. Rakhabdars still stuck to their root and potato/ egg was never ever used in Biryani. Hence, be prepared to have Biryani here without them. 

But, to make up to the loss of that, Royal Biryani is THE best in Kolkata if one is looking for subtleness in it. Its mild and fragrant and meat pieces are so tender so that they just melt in the mouth. The rice is long-grained and non-greasy yet having that aroma. Now, I can‚Äôt describe it. Just one suggestion. Do yourself a favor and have it‚Ä¶..¬†

Along with the Biryani, we had Chicken Rahmi Tikka, Fish Tikka Kabab and Mutton Burra Kabab. Chicken Rashmi Tikka was good, nothing extra-ordinary. Good, succulent pieces, lightly spiced- my son loved them. Fish Tikka was brilliant. It was spicy yet not fiery. They use Fresh water Vetki and portion size is quite good. 

But Mutton Burra Kabab (above) was brilliant. Boneless Mutton Chunks were soft yet chewy and that gave them their identity. Spread a little dhania chutney and heaven is yours. Too bad they do not serve wine here‚Ä¶.. (I knew that, didn‚Äôt I ? )¬†

Next we ordered some Roomali roti and along with, came the famous Mutton Champ and Mutton Pasinda Kabab. We‚Äôll start with the champ. Mutton champ is what Royal is mainly famous for (really ??? ) and its good. But, lots of bone pieces come is a dish and every one a while I needed to sort it out- which I didn‚Äôt like. On the good part, it was not extremely oily and its difficult to figure out where the gravy finishes and the meat starts or is it the other way round ? 

The Mutton Pasinda Kabab (above) was, on the other hand, was a revealation. It was boneless mutton chunks in a thick brown gravy. Quite hot, yet enjoyable. We just loved it. One suggestion for both the dishes, once you‚Äôre through, wipe the bottom of the plate clean with your roomali roti and a heavenly smile will come to you‚Ä¶ Amen. ¬†

Well, so, we were mostly done yet the waiter didn‚Äôt allow us to leave unless we have a slice of their ishpecial Shahi Tukra. and boy, was he right‚Ä¶..

A fat, thick piece of sliced bread soaked in rabri and sprinkled with dry fruits- somebody has to be really really insane to ignore that. Neither did we. Statutory warning. Order this dish before you start your meal because this thing tends to get over extremely fast and you‚Äôll be the one to lose out. ¬†

We could hardly move and probably needed a help to get out from the table. All the items were extremely moderately priced, then again when could money buy happiness ? 

Do yourself a favor and before you even start discussing the Biryani scene in Kolkata, visit this place. In all probability, opinions will change.

The Chaap however was really good!! Yet, you can get the same feel at Shiraz so nothing extraordinary.

My savior of the day would be the firni I ordered while leaving which was the best I've had..
So Food (OVR of 3.5/5) : biryani 1.5/5 chap 4/5 firni 5/5.

Hospitality (1/5) the waiter saw my bottle of thumsup and threatened me that if i drink from it they'll accuse me of drinking alcohol (WTF) and Normally at arsalan or zeeshan they politely tell me not to have outside food or beverages but they were so rude. and another guy came forward and shook my bottle saying "Nahin! Nahin! Allow nahin" I mean come don't destroy the fizz!!!

So In the end it was so not worth it.

My final viewpoint would be-

Arsalan > Aminia > Shiraz > Zeeshan ~ Rahmania~Nizam's > Amber > Oudh 1590 (Raan Biryani ^_^)   > India Rest. > Biryani Company > Alishaan Biryani House ('tis really cheap since it is roadside dhaba types) > Royal India Hotel (Yes the biryani was that disgusting)

only go for chaap and roti/naan if its near your house :-)

For years I've heard, 'Royal-er biriyani khash ni, tahole r ki kheli'... So finally came my chance to taste the big daddy of Calcutta biriyani...

We had Reshmi Malai Kebab, Royal Mutton Biriyani, Royal Mutton Chaap and Firni...

Decor - The AC dining hall upstairs was quite shabby with unclean tables, wobbly chairs etc. But then, I didnt expect anything more.

Service - Serving time is impressive.
The kebabs came pretty fast inspite of a nearly full house.

Now to the Food -

Reshmi Malai Kebab - Okay. Nothing special.

Royal Mutton Biriyani - Surprisingly nothing special. Just like the biriyani of Arsalan minus the Aloo, which is an absolute negative point to me. & I always knew potato is the trademark of an authentic Calcutta biriyani.

Royal Mutton Chaap - It had the perfect blend of spices but nothing special.

Firni - Well I wont say its the best firni I ever had, but its wayyyyyy better than the ones served at Zeeshan/Arsalan/Shiraz.

Value for Money - Inexpensive.

Probably all the exaggerations about Royal got my expectations soaring, that the food here couldn't match. Overall the food is okay. But if you live in south calcutta like me, you dont have to travel this far. The restaurants at Park Circus could jolly well satisfy your biriyani craving.

##

2015-02-04 08:38:30
Debankan Banerjee
681052
4.0
A vintage restaurant featured in the 'legendary' category of zomato, you can understand why wouldn't I give a long introduction to it. It's been an important pillar of the famous biriyani culture of Kolkata with their trademark 'no potato biriyani ' and not to mention they make one of the better chicken / mutton chaps in the city. After having the biriyani umpteen number of times finally my review goes.
Ambiance - it shouts the smell of old Kolkata. The lost system of cabin dining, the classic red uniforms, the same old Muslim waiters who had mastered the art of it over ages, it may not be the plush chic restro, but if you like old school you will like it.
2. Food - afterall that's why everyone comes here. We ordered 
1. Mutton Biriyani / Chicken Biriyani - That beautiful blend of saffron and white rice, beautifully cooked soft succulent pieces of meat, and that subtle aroma which I so miss in Ncr biriyanis. Eat it..you won't regret.
2. Mutton Chap - Because they are the best. Period. Not to spicy, not very mild, you won't find a better thing to polish away your biriyani plate.
3. Tandoor Roti - Soft fluffy rotis, this thing remains same pan India almost. 
4. Firni - Mughlai khana deserves a mughlai dessert. Firni, the moghul's fine inclusion in Indian kitchen by using ground rice flour and milk to make this thick flavourful bowl of wonder is another must have dessert in Royal.
Service - Fast, smooth order taking, absolutely hasslefree.
Price - very much fairly priced.
Overall, a place to visit definitely simply for their biriyani and chap.

##

2014-11-15 18:10:46
Pradip Sampat
2901988
5.0
Kolkata Kalling!!!

A trip to Kolkata is not a trip till you visit the Royal Indian Hotel in Rabindra Sarani! Located on the Chitpur Crossing, this restaurant does not need any introduction to the average Bengali! Get into a taxi from any part of Kolkata and all you need to say is 'Royal Hotel' and that's it!

Traffic is an issue in the area and also being the tramway, expect delays to reach the restaurant. Don't be disappointed with the queues outside the place since it's just the parcel queue. 

The biryanis available here are a hit across this part of India and believe it or not but does not contain potatoes, a staple feed everywhere and other vegetables. It's just the rice and the meat depending on the Biryani you order. The rice is a consistent one inch or longer Basmati Rice with the right amount of spices. If you are the health conscious type, let me add, there is hardly any amount of oil and is just smooth!

Also do remember to ask for the daily special and try it with the piping hot Roomali Roti. I tried the Mutton Pasanda along with the Roomalis and would give a 5 star ranking for the same. Also they do have a family room upstairs but expect delays in getting a table. They also have an AC section but again the waiting time. With the whiff of the Biryani in the air, it would be difficult to control your hunger. Jump into the first available seat and relish your meal. 

A must visit each time and every time!

427768
4.0
On one of our 'Rediscover The City' days two of my friends and I came to the restaurant we have heard so much about but never had a chance to visit. If you are a stranger to the streets of North Calcutta then it will take you quite some time to locate this place. Luckily, we took a tram and it dropped us right in front of it. We were immediately let down by the look of the restaurant. We took a table in the AC dining room as the non-ac one was not appropriate for three girls.
Now coming to food, we had high hopes as recently one of our equally food-loving friends had tasted the biriyani from here and said it was heavenly. And boy, was he right! When I put the first spoon of mutton biriyani in my mouth it seemed like I have died and come to some kind of biriyani heaven. It is arguably the best one can find in Kolkata. Not too oily, not too spicy, it had the right amount of scent. And the mutton was so soft! We also ordered a side of Chicken Chaap which was equally yum. Of course, these were not enough for gluttons like us. A full Chicken Tandoori was then asked to bring. The huge pieces of chicken that we got for such a nominal price was unbelievable! Lastly, I had to have phirni, which was good.
Food - 4
Service - 3
Decor - 1.5

2014-07-24 12:56:22
Mrinalini Sil
277392
4.0
No,its not a very hep or sophisticated place to dine in, it doesn't have a fancy environment or a posh ambience . It is located in one of the busiest and noisiest streets of Kolkata ¬†. The A.C dining hall on the first floor is clean but has nothing extravagent about it. That is, the impression until the plates of food arrive in front of you. And then its pure bliss in the form of a light aromatic Biriyani which is so tasty that you can actually eat it without any sides. It has a hint of pepper which will last on your palate for quite some time. The mutton in the biriyani is soft and tender, as well cooked as possible. We incidentally took side plates, Mutton Chap which was good but nothing striking about it, and Mutton Pasinda, which was probably the highlight of the evening. It is a boneless mutton preperation, mildly spicy with a very authentic Mughlai taste, not as greasy as the Chap and sings beautifully well with the light Biriyani. It makes your day.We wanted Shahi Tukra for desert but beacuse it was not available we had to satisfy ourselves with a Firni, which was once again good but nothing outstanding.We visited the place during Ramzan , and the entire area was bubbling with life and people. It definitely is a place to be if one seeks for authentic Mughlai flavours and the old world charm of this city.

The Royal Chicken Biryani : Melting Chicken with finest basmati cooked to its perfection in charcoal fire

Hats off to the Royal Indian Hotel :)
