4.5
To start with,i am very nostalgic about this place.Since childhood i heard stories from my father that the name that comes after the word biryani was ROYAL..This is one of the most popular biryani joints in kolkata.
Situated at one of the most busiest place in Kolkata i.e Burrabazar, the best way to get to this restaurant is to get down at M.G.Road crossing and take the route towards howrah,stop at the Chitpur and Harrison road crossing and take a left and walk for around 2mins u will find the name of ROYAL on ur right hand side.
The first thing u would notice at the entrance of Royal is a man cooking chanp and mutton tikia the aroma of which will surely drive u crazy.
It has a ground floor section and also a first floor section.the first floor section has an AC and a non AC section..the ground floor is generally conjested so it is suggested to take the first floor if u r going with your family..
Now coming to the main thing i.e the food,the biryani that is served here is not the usual ones we have i.e it will not have a potato or an egg.the biryani served here is spicy and is different.
The dishes that we ordered were:-
1.Chicken Biryani
2.Chicken Chanp
3.Mutton Tikia
4.Rumali Roti 
5.Salad
6.Shahi Tukda
I wanted to take pictures of food that we ordered it was in my mind.But as the foods were served i forgot everything and pounced on it..
What i felt that the rice was a bit overcooked but the taste was really good.it was spicy awadhi style biryani that is served here and not at all dry.the chanp as we all know is the speciality of ROYAL so its the best here no doubt about it.the tikia is also good atleast i like Royal's tikia the most as it is soft and cooked to perfection.And since it was a sunday so i ordered Shahi Tukda.Shahi tukda is available only on wed,fri and Sunday..it was beautifully garnished and tasted good....Our total bill was Rs.383..Overall it was a very good experience at royal..the waiter was also very attentive..But what may concern many people is the ambience.So if u r not concerned about the ambience you should surely visit this place.
No doubt that the food really comes from heaven.This is a place everyone should visit.And i am eagerly waiting for my next visit to this place.

Well in my last review i did not post any picture..So after a lot of frequent visits since my last review i am here to mention some other items i had..
1. To start with..Its The RAMZAM SPECIAL HALEEM which is avaiable only during ramzan month and to my opinion its the best haleem i had in the city..A proper mixture of spices and dal and the mutton pieces are tender and soft enough to melt in your mouth..
2.¬†Mutton Keema is another item i had which is a worth mention..The taste is awesome..Its rich and spicy enough and have it with roomali roti to get its actual taste..The mutton keema has a huge demand hence it wont be available in the evening..
3.The Nargisi Kofta..Its basically boiled Egg surrounded with keema and fried then dipped in the gravy..Available only on Wednesday and Saturday..Not veryyyy tasty or anything special..But yes it is beautifully made and gravy is very light but on the oily side..
4.The Mutton Chaap..Needless to say as its the speciality of ROYAL..

5.Last but not the least THE MUTTON PASINDA KEBAB..this item will really drive you crazy..the boneless Mutton is a treat to have..Again the boneless mutton pieces are tender,juicy and cooked to perfection..it tasted different and trully awesome..Its available only on wednesday,friday and sunday..On wednesday and friday its available after 1pm..And on sunday its available after 6pm..SO DONT MISS IT..

2014-05-12 02:40:43
Kingshuk Sett
402435
4.5
This place evokes nostalgia. The 1st ever biriyani I ever tasted was from this place, even though I never visited there as a child (my father got parcels and we had it in home).  Since my teenage days I have visited this place on numerous occasions and the last one being 6 months back. So its quite apt to write my 1st review in Zomato for this place. 
Their quality has deteriorated I must admit, but the essence of their signature dishes remains the same. The 2 most popular and my personal favorites are mutton biriyani and mutton chaap. 
The biriyani they prepare is a 100% Awadhi biriyani without the quintessential potato and the egg which one finds in the Calcutta biriyani.  Legend has it that the founder of ‚ÄúRoyal‚Äù was the actual khansama of the ousted nawab of awadh, ‚ÄúWajid Ali Shah‚Äù. Now Calcutta biriyani is an offshoot of the Awadhi biriyani, the added ingredients being potato and egg. The aroma and flavours of the biriyani is so enriching that it totally compensates for the potato and egg. It is unique and quite stunning.
The 2nd Signature dish of ‚ÄúRoyal‚Äù is their mutton chaap, which is dry and peppery and goes best with the rumali rotis. Again this is unique because it does not have gravy unlike other restaurants.

The other dishes are also quite good especially the keema and pasinda. 

Overall this place is a must visit for any true blue calcuttan if one is not too fussy about ambience.

While Poorna has openly stated that she does not feel  the chanp of this eatery is the best in town yet says that  it good enough, one bite and I realize , that  for me it is the best in town again. and why? Thick gravy stuck tot he chicken , no oil , soft meat flavours which cannot be expressed in words. I do not need further explanation. 

Too bad the place is a bit off the route for me but if I am having biriyani from now on there can only be one place I am heading to. 

When I told my father I had visited Royal he felt nostalgic but I got my share of scolding for going to that area but then again I told him I had a catwoman with me . So boys and girls ladies and gentleman do try and go in a group even if you want to pick up a few items . That is my advice , whether you take it or not is up to you.

2013-12-08 20:52:39
Arijit.dodul
1477155
4.5
My first visit to Royal was when I was in school; I remember that we took a tram from Howrah Stn to Chitpur. And, I distinctly remember the dishes we ordered- Mutton Chanp, Rumali Roti and Mutton Biriyani. The biggest tribute I can give to that place and its dishes is that I still go there to have the Mutton Chanp, Biriyani and Firnyi- it simply brings back the memory of my very first visit there. The Mutton Chaanp is simply a work of art here; the mutton is more shredded than in lump pieces and is pretty dark and menacing in its looks but the taste is awesome and delicious. If one is not concentrating on eating it with the complete attention it deserves (which is basically impossible!!) then the chaanp tends to get a tad dry at the end of the 2 nd roti but nevertheless, the plates are all generally spotlessly clean without a trace of oil or anything else at the end of the meal. I guess that is enough testimony. The biriyani does not have alu/potato which is different from the general Biriyani that is served elsewhere in the city. But, the mutton is simply superbly spiced and perfectly cooked for the right softness yet the fibrous nature of the meat remains.  I also enjoy the Mutton Tikiya and the Mutton Korma there; both of which are perfect renditions of the mutton in the best of taste and panache. It is best to go during lunch time which extends up to late afternoon of 3-4 pm. The ground floor is pretty crowded and not really conducive for a group or a family; it is better to go to the First Floor in that case but be a little careful with the steep steps. One of the best ways to see and feel Kolkata is to have a walk through the lanes by the Nakhoda Masjid and look at the Chikan fares on the streets or my personal preference, take a tram..... unforgettable.

##

2013-10-22 15:56:54
Yummraj
55295
4.5
In a nutshell:

Legendary in the 1950s & 60s, this eatery impressed YUMMRAJ with quite a few dishes. 

Short Description ‚Äì in case u r in a hurry:

I have of course heard the name of Royal many times but never had really taken the trouble to go there due to the mixed reviews I used to get. People wud say that ‚Äòit used to b good but not that good now. Arsalan is better‚Äô etc. So when my friend & connoisseur of Mughal food recommended me to go here, I decided to take the plunge.

Well, for us, to have good food no amount of challenge is a challenge. We chose a weekday (assuming it wud be relatively less crowded) & drove to chitpur. Trying to park the car there can b a nightmare. So it is prudent to take public transport / go in a car with a driver.

The restaurant is in different levels. It has a large signage outside & is difficult to miss. Even if u miss it, everyone there knows about Royal. So to find the place is not a big deal I must say. 

The Ground floor is (my version) Economy Class. It has fans to cool the diners, has tables & chairs in a congested way & is full of activity all day long. This is infact where u get the real; feel of the place. A part of the Kitchen is also visible from here. 

A narrow flight of stairs takes one up to level 2 which is a bit more ‚Äòfamily restaurant‚Äô kind. This one is non airconditioned. When I say narrow I mean only one person can go in one direction. The rest wait at the other end of the staircase. I guess there r close to 30 steps in the staircase & that makes for a good little workout before u delve into buckets of greasy food.

A level above is the airconditioned section which is more of a regular A/C restaurant feel. Waiters here r more seasoned & are pretty trained to deal with people who r paying more for the same food that is available in all three levels.
The menu card was short & crisp ‚Äì 2 pages & focused. It just listed the iems. No description, no pictures of dishes. 
There was an interesting writeup on the back of the menu card.

I loved the taste of the food in general. Liked some curries more than the fabled Biryani. The dish & all others at this restaurant was made with ‚Äòdalda‚Äô - they tasted good but wud solidify if not eaten hot. Surely not the best thing for health but who cares about all that while being nice to the tastebuds. I usually look forward to opportunities in the next few days to workout extra & burn the extra fat.

Detailed Description ‚Äì In case u have the Time to NJOY reading:

We started our lunch with Mutton champ & roti. This is a signature dish of royal. It had numerous small pieces of mutton some boneless & some with rib bones. It had a peppery, grainy, minimalistic gravy that was dark brown in color. The taste was very spicy, robust & very rustic. Super loved it & rate it 4.75/5

Post that we moved to Mutton tikia. These were large tikias, the size of burger patty. These were made the traditional way ‚Äì Not machine minced but hand minced. That was evident from the taste & texture of the meat. Thus the patty was very juicy inside & had robust taste & flavors. I rate it 4.5/5

Mutton handi was a mutton gravy dish & was just outstanding. There was makhana & full red chillies visible in the gravy. Rest of the masalas had been well cooked & none retained their original look. The presence of a lot of onion juice had ensured that the gravy had a mild natural sweetness. The balance of the dish was super awesome ‚Äì salt, sweet & hotness. It being one of the best dishes I had this Pujo I rate it very high at 4.9/5.

Mutton biryani was different from the version that Shiraz & Arsalan have. The long grains of aromatic rice were soft but not melt in the mouth. The biryani was greasier & spicier than the one at Shiraz. The spice mix was a tad different & there was a ‚Äòhot‚Äô aftertaste. There was no aloo or boiled egg in the Biryani. One plate Biryani had only 1 piece of mutton. Arsalan has an option of ‚ÄòSpecial Biryani‚Äô that has 2 pieces in 1 plate. No such option was available at Royal. I rate the rice of the Biryani 4/5
The lone mutton piece in the Biryani was quite big though. It was just outstanding. It was super soft,melt in the mouth & totally non-fibrous. It had an intense taste to it. I rate the mutton in the Biryani 4.8/5

Overall the flavors of the meats, spices & rice intermingled well & we were happy with our Biryani. I rate this 4.4/5

For desserts we tried Phirni. This was thick, subtle in flavors & unidirectionally sweet ‚Äì Not too sweet. The extent of cashew & milk was less as compared to the best I have had. I rate it 3/5

We also tried Shahi tukra for dessert. It was sweet but had a nice hint of salt in it. The base was of course bread & atop was a 1.5mm thick layer of inhouse made milk cream. The shahi tukra was garnished with super super thin slices of almonds that started looking like kesar from a distance. Liked it quite a bit & rate it 4/5

Overall the rating of food at Royal averages out to 4.25/5. I am super keen to get back there to try the other dishes. Till then alvida‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶..

##

2013-07-20 21:45:51
Debarghya Roychowdhury
203741
4.0
If Arsalan is the Akbar of Biryanis, royal can be regarded as the Babur, one of the forerunners in this area in Kolkata. Located in Bara Bazaar, the setting of the restaurant is a scene out of old-world Calcutta - Calcutta, mind you, not Kolkata. That makes all the difference in my opinion.

I don't know if the practice is still alive, but one of the tales you'd hear about this place is the way the cooks would cook their tikias. The cooks would release the meat into huge 'kadhais' of hot oil, and then...wait for it...turn them with their bare hands to cook them overall, an ability born from years of cooking in the kitchen. I just wish I had the means to verify this urban legend.

Expect to be surprised by the Biryani in this place - solely because of the lack of the potato in it. However, if you think that this means a reciprocal increase in quantity, you'll be mistaken. Portions are not grand, but the taste of the Biryani more than makes up for it. The Biryani is spiced, offering a new dimension to the genre of Kolkata Biryani that is so famous among the citizens of the City of Joy. 

And to go with it - The Royal Chaanp. And I'm not even sure if that's the actual name or an adjective (which it definitely deserves). Best Chaanp I've ever eaten, period. Even Arsalan cannot compare. The Pasinda is very tasty as well, but the chaanp is what leaves me with fond memories. The Nargisi Kofta is another recommendation - oh, and their Rotis (both Tandoori and Roomali) are quite decent.

I'm not going to comment on the rest of the food simply because I haven't tried much else and the above is what makes Royal famous anyway. I'm going to finish with the Firni, which is awesome and just the right consistency and taste. 

Go to Royal for the Biryani and Chaanp and a slice of Calcutta. Just be sure not to gorge on too much food - one thing I remember courtesy of my childhood visits is that the stairs in that place are killer. Beware, because Humayun probably took a tumble down one of those kinds of stairs and kicked the bucket after a good meal and a lazy read at the library. Don't go the same way!

Ok let me begin by saying that the biggest problem is finding the place itself...
Located in the Barabazar area rather on the Chitpur road on Rabindra Sarani a place famous cause it is a locality with the Nau Khuda Masjid, Union Chapel and a Mandir of a Rajasthani Goddess (I am sorry I forgot the name)..However it is closes to the Nau Khuda Masjid...
How to reach there (my preferred way since the other times have been through lanes and bylanes to reach the place half of which I cannot recognize anymore) is by getting down at M.G Road metro station and asking anybody how to reach either Nau khuda Masjid or Royal....Chances are they will know both the places and you will reach easiest...
Now the menu is small but there are some things that you must try. 
The ones from Mutton that you must try are:
1)Nargisi Kofta
2)Mutton Pasinda kabab
Both of the above are available on specific days so select the one available on that very day
Also give the Mutton Stew a try am not betting on it to be your favourite but chances are you will like it.
There might be something wrong with the menu given in the Zomato site because it shows a higher rate for the non A.C one than the A.C one am not so sure about that.
Now the specialities...
The reason you must go to Royal for are the Royal Biryani, The Royal Chap and the Firni.
Let me attack them one by one...
The biryani is AWE-FREAKING-SOME not that I have not had better but definitely goes down into the top few in Kolkata...The thing which goes wrong in this...The Biryani aaloo is missing...Yes I agree you will not get aloo outside Kolkata in Biryani but then this is Kolkata Biryani and must have aloo...Absolutely must...  Also the quantity is a bit on the lesser side compared to the few top names and you will want to have more but once you have it and order another you tend to feel even a Rumali Roti is too big to be handled...Thus maybe a little marginally more rice was expected. However they add some spices which makes it a bit different and I am not sure about this but a friend of mine whose family has been a regular since ages and who have this as their special hotspot tend to say that they are so regular that all waiters know her father and uncle an despite uncle having asked them they had not divulged the spices...They had supposedly said to uncle that it is something their wives make at home and something they will never share with the world.. Now that Hyderabadi Biryani has gone for a copyright maybe they can try it too if the story stands true since then it would show a strange sense of loyalty, expertise and commitment.
The Royal Mutton chap is awesome and sticks to its name and fame of being the best...Though Arsalan comes very close but I would still prefer Royal's. However it is very bony and the fact that Arsalan waiters care to check for giving fewer bones is the thing I feel is the reason Royal gives Arsalan a choice to even come close...Otherwise this would have been the best without a doubt and I still feel maybe they are that good.
The Firni here is the best Firni in town and it is a bit yellowish in colour and soft and tender and makes you want more and more....Give it a try....
Trying it Amitabh Bacchan style when he promotes Gujrat
Ekbaar toh khao Royal mein
However, since Ta'am came into the whole consideration (the restaurant beside Priya) stuff have changed and they have stiff competition since I believe now the Mutton Irani chaap at Ta'am is better than that at Royal and the Firni is equally good if not better. The only reason you can choose Royal over Ta'am is the lesser price otherwise everything else is so much better and the Biryani is also good...
I know of late I have been comparing most Mughlai restaurants to Ta'am but they really deserve it. I wish the owner(s) of Ta'am had given me some extra discount considering I am a student and such a huge fan plus promoter of their Restaurant.
Thus if I have given Ta'am a 4.5 it should be around the 4 mark on ratings but still give Royal a try....I am sure you will not be disappointed by Royal and though you may not feel Royal but you will definitely feel great

##

2013-05-19 15:12:08
Somnath Basu
676598
4.0
Many places in Calcutta are said to serve good biriyani, but I prefer Royal primarily on account of the quality of the food and the slight differences from the other Mughlai restaurants of the city.

Royal is difficult to get to unless one is familiar with the one-way system on Rabindra Sarani (Lower Chitpur Road). The best way to get there is to come down Mahatma Gandhi Road, get off transport at the M. G. Road - Rabindra Sarani crossing and walk the two minutes it takes to reach the place. The upper floor is kept for casual diners - the ground floor serves daily customers, and sometimes it is nicer to sit downstairs in order to soak in a different kind of ambience.

The two items that are standard orders here are the biriyani and the chaap. The Chicken Chaap is actually preferable to the mutton version.  However, the cut of meat that lands on your plate is dependent on luck; sometimes, you get more bone, sometimes, more meat.

The biriyani, however, is very well made. It is best eaten in winter, when the quality of the meat is best. Royal is also unique in that it is one of the few restaurants that do not put potatoes in their biriyani. Most biriyani-eaters do not know that potatoes are not an integral part of biriyani - in fact, potatoes were added in order to save costs in the household of the exiled Nawab of Oudh, whose court pretty much introduced biriyani to Calcutta. There are other items that are also very good. The Nargisi Kofta is only sold on Wednesdays and Saturdays, but it is worth it - essentially, a Mughlai version of a Scotch Egg.

The service is quick, but the waiters could do with a little less brusqueness. The quality of the food is what draws me to this place, and I would like to go back again.

I chose to have a late lunch at Royal on a day i decided to have an affair with an older Kolkata....after a languid stroll through park street cemetery and then through larger part of the Dalhousie area took a tram to Burrabazar in search of the renowned biriyani and chanp!!! the tramride itself felt like going back in time...winding through crowded street and fighting for every turn it has to take, it took me to my destination. Went to the upstairs restaurant and sat at one of those isolated cabin for "Family". without so much as a glance at the menu i ordered my fare. And it arrived.
A lot is being said about the drop in quality and rise in price. but on that day nothing could have made me feel quite as nostalgic as that plate of biriyani and chanp!! true the quantity was small, biriyani on the bland side (Considering the same at Arsalan), the meat portion abysmal. but the taste i felt have remained grossly the same. the moment i tasted it it transported me back to my college days, friends shouting and fighting for the last rice grain and shred of meat!!!
I know this is not a place fit for my nostalgic babble, but my point is, sometimes a place like this, degrading, decaying perhaps, with not a zilch of an ambiance, is a true reminder of what good food is all about. Good memories.

2012-11-02 18:57:23
Shaunak Ganguly
248070
1.0
After hearing so much about this place for the last ten years or so I must say that it was a huge let-down to me.
There is almost nothing good & everything bad about the place.Starting with the location..it is tucked away in an obscure alley in Central Kolkata and is pretty hard to find.Then to go to the air-conditioned restaurant, you have to climb a steep flight of stairs which can be very cumbersome for the elderly or ladies.
The ambiance is anything but good with the restaurant being able to accommodate only a few and the seating arrangement modest at best.
I now come to the food because if that was good then I could have neglected the other problems I mentioned, but good Lord! I have eaten biriyani in most of the places in Kolkata but this one was really bad. It is not at all tasty..no spice..no oil..no nothing for that matter!..Its totally bland and if you are above 60 years old and have a digestion problem then only can you like this! The Royal Chaap was another thing I was looking forward to & all I got was a Boney piece served with Dalda!..& the salt added was way too much too..The Rumali Rotis were cold and as with everything associated with the place..not upto the mark..
The service is okay though they messed up things & gave me Chicken Biriyani instead of Mutton which again i got to notice much later thanks to the miniscule piece i had got!..
& finally the price..For all this crappy food I had to fork out 250+!..Goes without saying that its overpriced..considering how bad it is!..
To all my fellow foodies..stick to Shiraz and Arsalan guys..they are way way better!..

If some one is willing to take on the hustle and bustle of Chitpur, and the scarecity of parking space, this place is the most authentic place to have awadhi cuisine. Unlike Kolkata style biryani, ROYAL biryani does not have the Potato. It is extremly light in spices, but having all the aroma's of the Biryani. The Chicken tikka kabab in particular is a delight to mouth. It really melts in the mouth. The Mutton chap is exquisitely marinated and so soft that at times it falls off the bone. All the dishes are very very resonably priced. However the biryani quantities are a little lesser by 30%as served by other hotels.
